<review>Woah, so many juice options! Their root beer floats aren't bad either. I went here on a typical LA hot AF summer day and was super parched after riding my motorcycle. < review>
Nothing like a good old Raspado on a hot day. So refreshing and tasty. Made to order for each person. So many veritys of flavors and drinks with refills. Nice and happy staff and handicapped parking and access and table seating and public restrooms. Their prices are not that bad. A good place to visit throughout the summer and year round.</review>

< text>
I would recommend making a reservation as itâ€™s easy to spend a couple hours enjoying good company in their cozy outdoor setting, eating delicious and fresh sushi and drinks served with much attention to detail.

We tried to go impromptu for late lunch when we arrived in La Jolla and all their tables were either half way through their meal or reserved so we decided to come back another time; let me tell you that making a reservation was a breeze and the staff was super courteous over the phone.

The portions are smaller but typical of a more upscale restaurant and everything is top quality; to name a few, the toro melts in your mouth, the scallops have a delicate flavor and the warm miso makes you feel right at home.  Our server was sincerely friendly and knowledgeable about the fish they were serving that night. If youâ€™re drinking sake, you get to choose your own cup, which is a lot of fun, and our server was even knowledgeable about what kind of cup was better for what kind of sake.
I also loved how the chef thanks you for coming in Japanese as youâ€™re leaving. We had a great experience at Himitsu!< /text>

['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipP2ETEhqq1fajgzftGe7UxLTFjrX9G6vR6ACi85=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipP-t01tbvHX3VIohZbuo8h8JRhc55ws4-nrEPl1=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': <Response>None< /Response><name>Jay Keyes</name><GmapID>0x80dc03e376700407:0xe6521b675eaa605<//GmapID>< text>
Himitsu is a quaint restaurant in La Jolla Cove serving high-end sashimi and nigiri alongside a compact menu of small plates and rolls. My visits to Himitsu have provided a generous amount of excellent sushi, and a warm experience that has rivaled my sushi experiences in Tokyo. The space consists of an outdoor patio and a handful of sushi bar seats which you should hope to reserve when dining here. A strong social vibe pervades the small sushi bar, isolated in its own intimate solarium where one has the opportunity to know their chef and fellow diners.

Behind the sushi bar is Chef Mitsu Aihara, formerly of Sushi-Ota. If you are fortunate enough to sit at the sushi bar and have Chef Mitsu attend to you personally, you MUST order the omakase, as Chef Mitsu delivers one of the best and most innovative omakase experiences in San Diego, proving to be similarly skilled to his mentor, Chef Ota. A friendly character with a natural ability to effortlessly create Instagram-able food porn, Chef Mitsu takes the time to know the diner he is serving and customizes the omakase experience for that person -- I noticed I was getting slightly different sushi than he was serving the couple next to me who were also doing omakase. The fish came out fast-and-furious and, two hours into it, I finally needed to tap out after being served an ultra-rich hand roll containing uni, "melt-in-your-mouth" otoro, and salmon roe, for what seemed like my 25th course in.

Much of Himitsu's fish is flown in overnight from Japan, though some of it is locally-caught as well. A few of my favorites that aren't as popular at other sushi joints in San Diego included the buttery "Black Throat Sea Perch" and the naturally sweet "Triggerfish," topped with its own white, sticky liver when served nigiri-style.

As other reviews have noted, Chef Mitsu loves Japanese sardines, here served as both nigiri and sashimi, somewhat fatty and slippery in texture and with a clean but concentrated flavor of fish. This is a unique piece of sushi I've not had elsewhere that reminded me of Red Boat 40Â°N, a favorite fish sauce in my household.

Mid-way through my omakase, I was offered Shirako, which Chef Mitsu described as "an appetizer, like eggs." Since I've had Shirako before, I shot back, "don't you mean sperm?", and so ended the ruse, as my fellow diners at the bar all soured their faces at once, and I enjoyed my cod sperm sacs, here served raw in a ponzu sauce -- its creamy white blobs sharing both the texture and taste of the fried belly parts of whole belly fried clams, but without the deep-fried batter.

Other sushi I've had here has included Otoro, Chutoro, Marinated Blue Fin Akami, Local Spiny Lobster, Salmon Belly, Hamachi Belly, Uni, Stripejack, Raw Squid, Seared Squid with Shiso and Eel Sauce, Needlefish, Octopus, Razor Clam, Albacore, Ocean Eel, Kelp-Marinated Halibut, and Wagyu Beef. All have been served fresh and, at minimum, have met my expectations. Additionally, I've ordered the "Salmon JalapeÃ±o," similar to Nobu's famous "Hamachi JalapeÃ±o," but Himitsu's choice to use "candy-striped" salmon meat leads to a more dramatic presentation despite a slight loss of richness.

I'm admittedly a bit of a sushi snob, but I don't need to gorge myself at spendy outlets like Tadokoro, Kaito, or Ota to be satisfied. However, due to the overall dependability of these restaurants, their sourcing of supremely high-quality seafood, and the mouth-watering plates of sashimi served, I am often willing to spend a little extra. Himitsu is such a place I'll open my wallet up for, and should be considered to be in the apex tier of sushi restaurants in San Diego.<//text>

<text>Probably the best sushi I've had in years. Unlike most places they don't flaunt an obscene number of novelty rolls. Instead they focus on am excellent selection of lesser known fish. That's not to say that the favorites aren't there. Both their sake belly and hamachi belly were respectable and their o toro was easily the best I've ever had. And the uni (both the local San Diego and the Japanese) were phenomenal. But I was pleasantly surprised by the Japanese sardine, the black cod, and the golden eye snapper. All were very good. And the saba, though not pickled like the rest I've had, was simply amazing.

Though we don't normally get desserts we opted to try the yuzu panna cotta and were blown away. Most japanese restaurants stick with simple fare like green tea ice cream, but not Himitsu. It was light and refreshing and a perfect end to a perfect meal. I am completely fulfilled.

10/10<//text>< user_id>

<Review>I wish I could say I've had a purchase from here that lasted longer than a few months...or days in this case

2 times I've come in on different occasions to be sold items that have been defective. Whether it be cracked glass or just plain stopped working. They don't sell quality items unless you want to pay ungodly sums of money for the few brand name non glass devices.

Their staff is not up to date with modern Cannabis Culture technology, especially Dry Herbal vapes, Dabbing technology/Innovations, and most importantly...prices.

I'll give them a pass on a few things they've tried to push on me but ultimately when they say "Dude you're not gonna find anything that this doesn't do about the same." They mean than what they have in their store...

Unfortunately they're a needed evil in Camarillo because they have the largest selection without possibly having to order online and waiting. You'll pay in 2nd rate devices & materials and more than it's worth paying but sometimes you need things.

You cannot count on the employees to be honest so go in KNOWING what you want or the combination of lack of knowledge & wanting a sales commission check will sway them from helping you find what you're looking for. That or they just ignore what your interests are.

Just being honest.< /Review>< Time>

<date>1536986535960< /date><Rating>2</Rating>< Text>
Overpriced.  Sign on window says  "Beats Internet Prices " It doesn't say anything about restrictions.  I bought a mod unit and it was at full MRP. Afterward I found the same item on several online sites for  about 45% less.  They told me that the USB cable in the kit was for charging.  This is wrong! The batteries have to be charged in a separate unit.  Since the mod I bought was at the highest suggested retail price, about double the price online and I was inconvenienced and had to go back the next day to buy the battery charger I thought they should comp the charger.
The employee called her manager to see what he would do for me.
He said the statement on the window only applied to the manufacturer's online site.  Even  so,  they didn't beat their online price.  The store price was the highest/full price, the same as the online price.  That constitutes false advertising!
The manager offered me only 15% off the charger.  Terrible customer service, especially for a customer who spent about $250 the day before.
I will never go back to Wild Side.  I went to the one in Camarillo.
I advise everyone to avoid this store.  Shop online!!!
Since the customers (about 6 within 20 minutes) were spending on the average of only 5 - 10 dollars,  they really should have treated someone spending over $250 with a greater sense of appreciation and given me the $47 charger for free.  They had the chance to make a customer for life.  Instead they lost a customer forever!</Text>

< text>
Was looking for a Ninja 300 and saw a Craigslist ad that showed one "on sale" at this dealership. The sale price was $4199 for a 2014 Ninja 300 SE (a year old model mind you). Somehow after getting a quote that price skyrocketed to $5600. Apparently any lower would've lost them money, although the Yamaha R3 has something like a $500 profit already built-in to the MSRP so I'm assuming the Ninja 300 is similar with Kawasaki. Contra Costa Powersports in Pleasant Hill was able to match this so-called "sale price" with a brand new 2015 SE Ninja 300, which has an MSRP of $5200. Obviously I went the route of getting the 2015 considering I didn't have any ridiculous fees tacked on. Payed MSRP and sales tax at Contra Costa and that was it. Listing a bike as on sale and then tacking on $1400 worth of fees is a little crazy, especially for a 2014 model. I would advise anyone to go to Contra Costa Powersports in Pleasant Hill, it's only a little bit further away and they'll most likely give you a better deal than this dealership. If you're looking for a Ninja 300 specifically and want to pay way too much then you should go here, otherwise look at the 2015 models at Contra Costa and get a year newer model for the exact same price as this dealerships "sale price" for a 2014.<//text>

< review>
BEWARE of the merced toyota service department! I took my car in to have some recall work done and when I picked it up they proceeded to tell me my car needed $900-$1000 worth of repairs. They said I needed a transmission service(which I knew, I just wasn't going to pay dealership prices to have done), then they said I needed a new battery, new water pump and a new serpentine belt. Within a week I took my car to my regular mechanic, a shop in town that I can trust, to have the transmission serviced and have them give the car a thorough bumper to bumper check. I also specifically asked them to check the parts merced toyota told me needed to be replaced and everything checked out just fine! No repairs needed! It's been several months now and none of the supposed "bad" parts have failed or needed to be replaced. If your toyota needs repair work you're definitely better off going elsewhere. I won't go back here even for recalls. I would rather go to Fresno or Modesto for that stuff.<//review>
